الآيات التي أمر الله عباده فيها بأن يستعينوا بالله ، وبأن يعين بعضهم بعضاً
أما الاستعانة بالله : فكقوله تعالى : ( إياك نستعين ) - ( فاستعذ بالله الشيطان الرجيم (۱) ) - ( وقل ربي أعوذ بك من همزات الشياطين (۲) ) استعينوا بالله (۳) ) وتقديره : إن الاستعانة إنما تعقل في حق من يقدر على الفعل، لكنه لا يقدر على إتمامه وإكماله إلا بإعانة المعين . فلو لم يكن العبد قادراً على التكوين والتحصيل كانت إعانته ممتنعة ، فكان أمره بالاستعانة عبثاً . وأما الأمر بإعانة بعضهم بعضاً . فكقوله تعالى : ( وتعاونوا على البر والتقوى ، ولا تعاونوا على الإثم والعدوان (٤) ( ومن لم يقدر على الفعل أصلا فكيف يمكنه إعانة غيره على الفعل ؟
والجواب : مذهبنا : أن الملزوم للفعل هو مجموع القدرة والداعي . وذلك مشروط بإزالة الموانع، فإعانة الله لعبده . هو أن يزيل الموانع عن كون ذلك المجموع مستلزماً لذلك الأثر
وأما إعانة بعضهم بعضاً : فهو أنه من الجائز أن لا تكون قدرة الإنسان الواحد وداعيته كافية في استلزام ذلك الفعل . بل لا بد فيه من قدر أناس كثيرين ومن دواعيهم ، حتى يترتب على مجموع تلك القدر وتلك الدواعي ،
حصول ذلك الأثر . فزال الإشكال
The fourth type of the aspects of inferences related to [؟] from the verses in which God commanded His servants to seek help from God, and to help each other. As for seeking help from God: like His statement: 'You alone we worship and You alone we seek help' - 'So seek refuge with Allah from Satan the accursed (1)' - 'And say: My Lord, I seek refuge in You from the whisperings of the devils (2)' - 'Seek help from Allah (3)'. And its implication: Seeking help is only conceivable with respect to one who is capable of the action, but he cannot complete and perfect it except with the help of the Helper. So if the servant were not capable of creation and acquisition, his help would be impossible, so commanding him to seek help would be futile. As for the command to help each other: like His statement: 'And cooperate in righteousness and piety, and do not cooperate in sin and transgression (4)'. And whoever is not capable of action at all, how can he help another to act? The answer: Our school: that the necessary condition for the action is the combination of ability and motive. And that is conditioned by the removal of obstacles. So God's help to His servant is that He removes the obstacles from that combination entailing that effect. As for mutual help: it is that it is possible that the ability and motive of one human being are not sufficient to entail that action. Rather, there is need for the abilities of many people and their motives, so that the occurrence of that effect results from the totality of those abilities and those motives. So the problem is resolved.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer within a broader argument about proofs for human agency. The author cites Quranic verses commanding believers to seek help from God (isti'ana) and to help each other (i'ana). The objection is: if humans are not genuine agents (as some determinists hold), then commanding them to seek help is meaningless because seeking help presupposes some ability to act but needing assistance to complete it. Similarly, commanding mutual help would be absurd if humans have no power to act at all. The author's answer, representing the Ash'ari school, explains that the necessary condition for an action (al-malzum li'l-fi'l) is the combination of ability (qudra) and motive (da'ii). This combination is conditional upon the removal of obstacles (mawani'). God's help consists in removing these obstacles, thereby making the combination effective in producing the action. As for mutual help, often one person's ability and motive are insufficient; many abilities and motives must combine to bring about the effect. Thus the commands are rational because human ability, though not the sole cause, is a real component that can be supplemented by others and by God's removal of obstacles. The objection is thereby resolved.

Key Terms
استعانة (isti'ana)
إعانة (i'ana)
قدرة (qudra)
داع (da'ii)
موانع (mawani')
ملزوم (malzum)
استلزام (istilzam)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Ash'ari school denies any real human role in actions.
Correction: This passage shows that the Ash'ari school affirms human ability and motive as part of the necessary condition for action, though they require God's removal of obstacles and possibly others' help.

Checkpoint
According to the author's answer, what does God's help to His servant consist of?
A) Increasing his ability directly
B) Removing obstacles so that the combination of ability and motive entails the action
C) Creating the action entirely without human involvement
D) Giving him a new motive

Key Takeaway
The commands to seek God's help and help others are rational because human ability, while real, is often insufficient on its own; God and others provide necessary conditions for action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'Iyyaka nasta'in' in prayer, do you truly believe that your own efforts are a real component that needs God's removal of obstacles, or do you recite it as a mere formula? What would change in your daily actions if you took this literally?
?
Think of a good deed you attempted but failed. In light of this lesson, did you seek God's help expecting Him to remove obstacles, or did you assume your inability meant you were not meant to do it? How can you better combine your own ability with divine help next time?
?
This lesson teaches that mutual help works by combining multiple abilities and motives. Do you rely on others in your community for righteous actions, or do you isolate yourself? What is one specific area where you need to ask for help from others today?

The Mu'tazila's Argument from Capacity and Its Refutation
The author presents and refutes the Mu'tazila's argument from capacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila's argument that God's verses prove the servant creates his own actions, and the author's refutation by showing the argument leads to self-contradiction.

Core Idea
The verses do not prove human creation of actions; they are interpreted non-literally.

In this passage, the author presents a key Mu'tazila argument from the Qur'an regarding human capacity. They claim that if God does not burden beyond capacity, then humans must create their own actions. The author responds by showing that this argument actually leads to untenable consequences for the Mu'tazila themselves.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: objection, entailment, scriptural evidence, and answer.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila's core argument
Find the conditional: if servant not creator then burden beyond capacity. Note how they derive servant's creation.
3
Analyze the entailment explanation
Understand why they think servant cannot act if God creates the act, and how that leads to burden beyond capacity.
4
Examine the author's refutation
The author claims the Mu'tazila themselves must accept burden beyond capacity, so their argument fails. Note the reference to twelve aspects not detailed here.

النوع الخامس من استحلالات التهم بالقرآن وهو جميع الأدلة الدالة على أنه تعالى لم يكلف فوق الوسع والطاقة. قالوا: لو لم يكن العبد موجداً لأفعال نفسه، لكان تكليفه بالفعل تكليفاً بما لا يطاق، وهذا باطل، فذاك باطل. بيان الملازمة: إنه إذا كان فعل العبد واقعاً بتكوين الله، فإن خلق ذلك الفعل لم يقدر على تحصيله لأن تحصيل الحاصل محال، وإن لم يخلقه لم يقدر العبد أيضاً على تحصيله، لأن قدرته غير صالحة للتحصيل. فثبت: أن العبد لو لم يكن موجداً لأفعال نفسه، لكان تكليفه تكليفاً بما لا يطاق. وإنما قلنا: إن ذلك باطل - لقوله تعالى: (لا يكلف الله نفساً إلا وسعها) ولقوله تعالى: (ولا يريد بكم العسر) ومعلوم: أن تكليف ما لا يطاق أعظم أنواع العسر. ولقوله: (وما جعل عليكم في الدين من حرج) ولا حرج فوق أن يكون الإنسان مكلفاً بما لا طاقة له به. والجواب: إنا بينا أن تكليف ما لا يطاق لازم على المعتزلة من الوجوه الاثني عشر التي ذكرناها وقررناها. فلا فائدة في الإعادة. وإذا كان كذلك فتحمل هذه الآيات على عدم الظاهرية.
The fifth type of [arguments from] the Qur'an: And it is all the proofs indicating that He, exalted, did not burden beyond capacity and ability. They said: If the servant were not the creator (mūjid) of his own actions, then his being burdened with the action would be a burden beyond what can be borne, and this is false, so that [proposition] is false. Explanation of the entailment: If the servant's action occurs by God's creation (takwīn), then if He created that action, the servant cannot acquire it because acquiring what already exists is impossible; and if He did not create it, the servant also cannot acquire it, because his power is not fit for acquisition. Thus it is established: that if the servant were not the creator of his own actions, then his being burdened would be a burden beyond what can be borne. And we only say that [burden beyond capacity] is false - due to His saying: 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity' (2:286), and His saying: 'and He does not intend difficulty for you' (2:185), and it is known that burdening beyond capacity is the greatest type of difficulty. And due to His saying: 'and He has not placed upon you in religion any hardship' (22:78), and there is no hardship greater than that a person be burdened with what he has no ability for. The answer: We have shown that burdening beyond capacity is a necessary consequence for the Mu'tazila from the twelve aspects that we mentioned and established. So there is no benefit in repetition. And if that is the case, then these verses are interpreted in a non-literal sense.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer format. It belongs to a section on arguments from the Qur'an. First, it states the Mu'tazila's objection: if the servant is not the creator of his own actions, then God's command to act would be a burden beyond capacity, which contradicts Qur'anic verses that deny such burden. The Mu'tazila provide an explanation of the entailment: if God creates the action, acquisition is impossible; if He does not create it, the servant cannot either. Therefore, they conclude that the servant must create his actions to avoid burden beyond capacity. The author then presents the answer: he claims to have already shown that burdening beyond capacity is actually a necessary consequence for the Mu'tazila themselves from twelve aspects (not detailed here). Therefore, their argument is self-defeating, and the verses are to be interpreted non-literally (i.e., not in their apparent meaning denying burden).

موجد
تكوين
تحصيل
الملازمة
الآيات
الظاهرية

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author denies the apparent meaning of the verses entirely.
Correction: The author only says the verses are interpreted non-literally in this specific context because the Mu'tazila's argument leads to self-contradiction.

Checkpoint

A) That God does not burden beyond capacity, so the servant must be the creator of his actions
B) That God burdens beyond capacity to test humans

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila's argument from capacity is refuted by showing it leads to a contradiction, requiring a non-literal interpretation of the relevant Qur'anic verses.

?
The author interprets these verses non-literally in response to a theological argument. Are there verses in your own understanding that you have taken at face value without considering deeper contexts? What would it cost you to admit that your interpretation might not be the only one?
?
This passage shows a conflict between divine omnipotence and human responsibility. Where in your life do you attribute your actions to your own will, and where do you acknowledge God's control? Are you willing to examine whether your belief is consistent, or do you hold contradictory positions for comfort?

The Sixth Objection: Does God Will Evil Because He Creates It?
The author presents the sixth objection and its refutation using the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of the sixth objection and its preliminary refutation, distinguishing between God's creation and His will.

Core Idea
God creates evil but does not will it; evil is detestable to Him.

The author presents a logical objection from opponents who argue that if God creates evil, He must will it, which is impossible. He refutes it by showing that even the determinists (Jabariyya) accept that creation implies will, but then proves that God does not will evil because it is detestable, citing the Quran. This lesson explores the reasoning behind this objection and its refutation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection's conditional logic
Read the objection carefully: if God creates disbelief and sins, then He must will them; but willing evil is false, so the premise is false. Notice the conditional structure.
This is the standard Mu'tazili argument against divine creation of evil.
2
Examine the implication and the Jabariyya's agreement
The author explains why the Jabariyya accept the implication: they believe that creation necessitates will, both from general principle and from the specification of actions to particular times and places. Understand these two reasons.
The author uses the opponents' own logic against them.
3
See the refutation using Quranic evidence
The author cites Quran 17:38, which says evil is 'makruh' (detestable) to God. Something detestable cannot be willed because that would combine opposites. Notice that this is a preliminary refutation; full treatment comes later.
The key term here is 'المكروه' (detestable).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع السادس من وجهه القوم أن قالوا : لو كان الله تعالى موجداً للكفر والمعاصي ، لكان مريداً لها وهذا باطل فذاك باطل . بيان الملازمة : إن المجبرة ساعدوا على أنه تعالى لو كان خالقاً لأعمال العباد ، لكان مريداً لها. وبيان هذه المساعدة من وجهين : الأول : إنهم في مسألة إرادة الكائنات قالوا : لما ثبت أن الله خلق أعمال العباد ، وجب أن يكون مريدا لها . والثاني : أنهم قالوا إنه تعالى لما خصص بعض أفعاله ، بإحداثه في وقت معين ، ومحل معين ، مع جواز أن يخلقه في وقت آخر ، وفي محل آخر ، وجب أن يكون ذلك التخصيص لأجل الإرادة . فثبت : أنه تعالى لو كان موجداً لأفعال العباد ، لكان مريداً لها وبيان أنه تعالى غير مريد لها : قوله تعالى : ( كل ذلك كان سيئه عند ربك مكروها ) والمكروه لا يكون مراداً لامتناع الجمع بين الضدين. وتمام الكلام في هذا المقام ، والاستدلال بجميع الآيات التي يتمسكون بها في أنه تعالى غير مريد للقبائح سيأتي الاستقصاء فيه في مسألة إرادة الكائنات إن شاء الله
The sixth type from the argument of the people: They said: If God Most High were the creator of disbelief and sins, He would be willing them, and this is false, so that is false. Explanation of the implication: The Jabariyya agreed that if He were the creator of the actions of servants, He would be willing them. And explanation of this agreement from two aspects: First: Regarding the issue of the will of created things, they said: Since it is established that God created the actions of servants, it is necessary that He be willing them. Second: They said: Since He Most High specified some of His actions by bringing them into existence at a particular time and a particular place, despite the possibility of creating them at another time and another place, that specification must be due to will. So it is established: that if He were the creator of the actions of servants, He would be willing them. And the proof that He is not willing them: His statement: 'All that is evil in the sight of your Lord is detestable' (Quran 17:38). And what is detestable cannot be willed due to the impossibility of combining opposites. And the complete discussion in this place, and the deduction from all the verses they use to argue that He is not willing evil, will come in detail in the issue of the will of created things, God willing.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage is an objection and a preliminary refutation. The author introduces the sixth objection from the opponents (likely Mu'tazila) against the Ash'ari position that God creates all actions, including evil. The objection is a conditional: if God creates disbelief and sins, then He must will them; but willing evil is impossible, so the premise is false. The author then explains the implication (mulazama): the Jabariyya (determinists) themselves agree that if God creates actions, He wills them. He provides two reasons for their agreement: first, from the established principle that God creates all actions, they conclude He wills them; second, from the observation that God specifies actions to particular times and places, which requires an act of will. Having established that creation implies will in their view, the author refutes the objection by proving that God does not will evil. He cites Quran 17:38, which describes evil as 'makruh' (detestable/abhorrent) to God. Something detestable cannot be willed, as that would combine opposites (willing and detesting) in the same object. The author notes that a full treatment of this topic, including all relevant verses, will follow later in the discussion on the will of created things.

مريد
المجبرة
الملازمة
إرادة الكائنات
المكروه
القبائح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if God creates evil, He necessarily wills it.
Correction: The passage clarifies that God does not will evil even though He creates it, as evil is detestable to Him.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why cannot God will what is detestable?
A) Because He is not able to will it.
B) Because it is impossible to combine opposites.
C) Because He only wills good.
D) Because the Jabariyya deny it.

Key Takeaway
The author refutes the sixth objection by showing that while creation may imply will in some contexts, God does not will evil because it is detestable, as per the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter evil in the world, do you ever question God's goodness? How does the truth that God does not will evil, but it is detestable to Him, reshape your trust in His wisdom? Write a prayer of submission to His decree while affirming His holiness.
?
Think of a sin you have committed. Did you ever rationalize it by saying 'It was God's will'? Based on this lesson, how should you view your sin now? Commit to taking full responsibility for your actions, knowing God detests your sin but still allowed it for a greater purpose.
?
How does the distinction between God's creation and His will affect your daily life? Are there areas where you blame God for your circumstances? What step can you take today to align your heart with the truth that God only wills what is good, even when you don't understand?

The Seventh Type: Proof from Recompense (Al-Qiyam)
The author presents the seventh type and cites recompense verses to prove human origination of acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'anic verses of recompense are used to argue that human actions are created by the servant, not by Allah.

Core Idea
Recompense verses prove humans create their actions because reward presupposes agency.

The author introduces the seventh type of argument (al-qiyam) and presents a scriptural proof. He cites numerous Quranic verses linking recompense to deeds, arguing that if the servant is recompensed for his actions, then those actions must be truly his own creation. This lesson unpacks that argument and its scriptural foundation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the logical structure: claim, inference, then supporting verses.
The passage is incomplete; focus on the argument presented.
2
Identify the claim and inference
The author claims that recompense verses prove the servant's actions are created by the servant. The inference is: if Allah recompenses based on deeds, then those deeds must be truly the servant's own doing.
This is the core logical move.
3
Examine the cited verses
List the verses mentioned. They all link recompense to what the servant 'did', 'earned', 'worked'. Ask: why does the author think these imply the servant creates his actions?
Hint: Otherwise recompense would be unjust.
4
Reflect on the larger argument
This is one of several arguments for human acquisition (kasb). Consider how it fits with the Ash'ari position that humans acquire actions while Allah creates them.
The author is building a cumulative case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع السابع القيم
الآيات الدالة على أنه متى فعل العبد فعلا ، فإنه تعالى يجازيه بفعل آخر وتقديره : أن نقول : القرآن يدل على أن العبد قد يفعل أموراً . متى فعلها . فإنه تعالى يجازيه عليها بأفعال أخرى ، ومتى كان الأمر كذلك ، وجب أن تكون تلك الأفعال واقعة بتكوين العبد ، لا بتكوين الله تعالى . بيان المقدمة الأولى : إن الآيات : ( جزاء بما كانوا يعملون ) - ( جزاء بما كانوا يكسبون ) - ليجزي الذين أساؤا بما عملوا ، ويجزي الذين أحسنوا بالحسنى - ( يا أيها الذين كفروا لا تعتذروا اليوم . إنما تجزون ما كنتم تعملون ) - ( ذلك بما قدمت يداك ) - ( اليوم تجزى كل نفس بما كسبت ) - ( فأخذتهم صاعقة العذاب الهون بما كانوا يكسبون ) هذه الآيات وأمثالها دالة على أن العبد إذا أتى بهذه الأفعال فإنه تعالى يجازيه
The seventh type: al-qiyam. The verses indicating that when the servant does an act, then He the Exalted recompenses him with another act. Its estimation: that we say: The Qur'an indicates that the servant may do things. When he does them, then He the Exalted recompenses him for them with other acts. And when the matter is like that, it is necessary that those acts occur by the servant's origination, not by the origination of Allah the Exalted. Explanation of the first premise: The verses: (A reward for what they used to do) - (A reward for what they used to earn) - 'To recompense those who do evil for what they did and reward those who do good with the best' - (O you who have disbelieved, make no excuses today. You are only being recompensed for what you used to do) - (That for what your hands have sent ahead) - (Today every soul is recompensed for what it earned) - (So the punishment of the humiliating lightning seized them for what they used to earn). These verses and their likes indicate that when the servant performs these acts, then He the Exalted recompenses him...
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh type (al-qiyam) and provides a proof from Quranic verses of recompense. The author argues that the Quran indicates that when a servant performs certain actions, Allah recompenses him with other actions. Consequently, those actions must be created by the servant himself, not by Allah, because otherwise the recompense would be for something the servant did not truly originate. The author then explains the first premise by citing several verses that speak of recompense for deeds, such as 'A reward for what they used to do' and 'Today every soul is recompensed for what it earned.' These verses, he says, demonstrate that when the servant performs these acts, Allah recompenses him. The passage is a clear example of how kalam arguments use scriptural evidence to support the Ash'ari position on human acquisition and divine justice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that recompense verses merely describe reward or punishment without implying anything about human agency.
Correction: The author argues that recompense logically requires that the servant be the true originator of the act; otherwise, it would be unjust to punish or reward for something one did not actually do.

Key Takeaway
Quranic verses that link recompense to human deeds are used to prove that humans are the true originators of their own actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Recompense Verses Prove Human Agency
The author enumerates Qur'anic recompense verses and argues that recompense implies human creation of actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'anic promise of recompense logically requires that human actions be created by the servant, not by God.

Core Idea
Reward and punishment only make sense if we truly own our actions.

The author presents a careful argument from Qur'anic verses on recompense. The logic is that if God rewards or punishes us for our deeds, those deeds must be truly ours—created by our own will, not by God. Otherwise, the entire system of divine justice would collapse.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once, then the translation. Notice how the author sets up two premises.
The passage uses a conditional structure: if servant does X, God does Y.
2
Identify the two premises
The first premise is that the Qur'an shows God recompenses actions. The second premise argues this necessitates the action being created by the servant.
The second premise is supported by two arguments.
3
Understand the first proof for premise two
If both the condition (servant's action) and reward (God's action) were God's actions, the servant would be excluded. The conditional would become 'when I do X, I do Y' which is not how God addresses us.
This highlights the difference between divine self-reference and divine address to creatures.
4
Understand the second proof
Recompense serves as incentive/deterrent, which requires the servant to have genuine capability to act or refrain. If God created the action, capability would vanish.
This links human agency to the purpose of divine commands.
5
Reflect on the implication
Consider how this argument defends human moral responsibility. The author's logic shows that without human creation of actions, divine justice becomes meaningless.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع السابع القيم: الآيات الدالة على أنه متى فعل العبد فعلا، فإنه تعالى يجازيه بفعل آخر. وتقديره: أن نقول: القرآن يدل على أن العبد قد يفعل أموراً، متى فعلها، فإنه تعالى يجازيه عليها بأفعال أخرى، ومتى كان الأمر كذلك، وجب أن تكون تلك الأفعال واقعة بتكوين العبد، لا بتكوين الله تعالى. بيان المقدمة الأولى: إن الآيات: (جزاء بما كانوا يعملون) - (جزاء بما كانوا يكسبون) - (ليجزي الذين أساؤا بما عملوا، ويجزي الذين أحسنوا بالحسنى) - (يا أيها الذين كفروا لا تعتذروا اليوم، إنما تجزون ما كنتم تعملون) - (ذلك بما قدمت يداك) - (اليوم تجزى كل نفس بما كسبت) - (فأخذتهم صاعقة العذاب الهون بما كانوا يكسبون) هذه الآيات وأمثالها دالة على أن العبد إذا أتى بهذه الأفعال فإنه تعالى يجازيه بأفعال أخرى. وبيان المقدمة الثانية: وهي قولنا: إن ذلك يقتضي أن لا يكون فعل العبد فعلا لله تعالى. فتقديره من وجهين: الأول: إنه لو كان الشرط فعلا لله تعالى، كما أن الجزاء فعله، لصار العبد من هذا الشرط والجزاء خارجاً من البين، ويصير التقدير كأنه تعالى يقول: إني متى فعلت الفعل الفلاني فإني أفعل بعده فعلاً آخر. إلا أن التغاير بين هذا الكلام وبين قوله أيها العبد إن أطعتني أثبتك، وإن عصيتني عاقبتك معلوم بالضرورة. الثاني: إنه تعالى إنما رتب هذه الأجزية على أفعال العباد ترغيباً لهم في الطاعات ومنعاً لهم عن المحظورات. وهذا إنما يفيد إذا كانوا قادرين على الفعل والترك، متمكنين من كل واحد منهما على البذل. وقد بينا: أنه لو كان موجد أفعال العباد هو الله تعالى لما بقيت هذه القدرة، وحينئذ يصير هذا الترغيب والترهيب عبئاً بالكلية. ومما يؤكد ذلك قوله تعالى: (وقالوا: اتخذ الرحمن ولداً، لقد جئتم شيئاً إداً، تكاد السموات يتفطرن منه وتنشق الأرض وتخر الجبال هذا: أن دعوا للرحمن ولداً) والاستدلال به من وجهين: الأول: إن ذلك القول لو كان مخلوقاً لله تعالى لصار الكلام ركيكا، لأنه يصير تقدير الكلام: تكاد السموات أجعلها منفطرة والأرضين أجعلها منشقة بما خلقت في العبد هذا الكلام، وأردته وقضيت به. ومعلوم: أن ذلك في غاية الركاكة. وأيضاً: فقوله: (لقد جئتم شيئاً إداً) نص في أن العبد هو الذي جاء بذلك الفعل. الثاني: إن الواحد منا إذا أنكر على غيره فعلاً، ثم أتى بمثله عد سفيها.
The seventh type, the values: The verses indicating that whenever the servant performs an action, then He, exalted, recompenses him with another action. Its estimation: that we say: the Qur'an indicates that the servant may do things; when he does them, then He, exalted, recompenses him for them with other actions. And when the matter is thus, it is necessary that those actions occur by the servant's bringing into existence (takwīn), not by the bringing into existence of God, exalted. Explanation of the first premise: Indeed the verses: 'A recompense for what they used to do' - 'A recompense for what they used to earn' - 'That He may recompense those who do evil for what they did, and recompense those who do good with the best' - 'O you who have disbelieved, make no excuses this day. You are only being recompensed for what you used to do' - 'That is for what your hands have sent ahead' - 'This day every soul will be recompensed for what it has earned' - 'So the punishment of a humiliating blast seized them for what they used to earn.' These verses and their like indicate that when the servant performs these actions, then He, exalted, recompenses him with other actions. And the explanation of the second premise: which is our statement: that this necessitates that the servant's action not be an action of God, exalted. Its estimation is from two aspects: First: if the condition were an action of God, exalted, just as the reward is His action, then the servant would be excluded from both this condition and the reward, and the estimation would become as if He, exalted, said: 'Whenever I do such-and-such action, then I will do another action after it.' However, the difference between this speech and His saying: 'O servant, if you obey Me I will reward you, and if you disobey Me I will punish you' is known necessarily. Second: He, exalted, only arranged these rewards on the actions of the servants as an incentive for them towards acts of obedience and a deterrent from prohibited things. And this only benefits if they are capable of action and inaction, able to perform each one. And we have shown: if the creator of the actions of the servants were God, exalted, this capability would not remain, and then this encouragement and deterrence would become entirely burdensome. And among what confirms that is His statement, exalted: 'And they say: The Most Merciful has taken a son. You have come with something monstrous. The heavens almost break apart from it, and the earth splits asunder, and the mountains fall in ruin: that they attribute to the Most Merciful a son.' And the inference from it is from two aspects: First: if that statement were created by God, exalted, the speech would become weak, because the estimation of the speech would become: 'The heavens I almost make them split apart, and the earths I make them split asunder, because of what I created in the servant of this speech, and I intended it and decreed it.' And it is known: that is extremely weak. Also: His statement: 'You have come with something monstrous' is explicit that the servant is the one who came with that action. Second: if one of us objects to another's action, then does the like of it, he is considered foolish.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage presents a proof that human actions are created by the servant (ʿabd), not by God. The author begins by stating that the Qur'an contains verses indicating that when a servant performs an action, God recompenses him with another action. From this, the author argues that such recompense implies the action must be the servant's own creation, not God's. This is broken into two premises. The first premise is supported by a list of Qur'anic verses (e.g., 'جزاء بما كانوا يعملون') which show God recompenses based on the servant's deeds. The second premise argues that this recompense structure would be meaningless if the servant's action were God's creation. The author provides two proofs for the second premise. First, if both the condition (servant's action) and the reward (God's action) were God's actions, the servant would be entirely removed from the equation, reducing divine speech to 'when I do X, I do Y'—which is clearly different from the imperative address to the servant. Second, the incentive/deterrent nature of recompense only works if the servant has genuine capability (qudra) to act or refrain; if God were the creator of the action, such capability would vanish, making the whole system pointless. Finally, the author reinforces the argument with the verse about those who say God has a son (sūrat Maryam 19:88-91). If that blasphemous statement were created by God, the Quranic rebuke 'you have come with something monstrous' would become self-referential and absurd. Moreover, if God rebukes such speech yet creates it, He would be guilty of the same fault. Thus, the verse confirms human agency.

Key Terms
جزاء
فعل العبد
تكوين
القدرة
الترغيب والترهيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that God creating all actions (including human actions) is compatible with divine recompense.
Correction: The author demonstrates that recompense logically requires the servant to have genuine agency; otherwise the conditional structure and the purpose of incentive/deterrent collapse.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why does the Qur'anic recompense for actions prove that those actions are not created by God?
A) Because God's actions are perfect and human actions are imperfect.
B) Because recompense implies the servant has capability (qudra) and choice; if God created the act, that capability would be negated.
C) Because the Qur'an explicitly states that God does not create human actions.
D) Because recompense is only for actions that are evil.

Key Takeaway
The Qur'anic promise of recompense logically requires that human actions be created by the servant, not by God, because otherwise the conditional address and the purpose of incentive/deterrent would be undermined.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Read the verses quoted: 'Recompense for what they used to earn.' If you truly believe your actions are your own, why do you still hesitate to take full responsibility for your choices? What would change if you treated every sin as something you created yourself, not God's decree?
?
The author says recompense only works if you are able to act or refrain. Where in your life are you acting as if you have no choice? What would it mean to genuinely own your ability to obey?
?
Imagine standing before God and hearing 'That is for what your hands have sent ahead.' Would you be able to say 'my hands did it'? If not, what are you waiting to change?

The Verse of the Son: A Further Proof
The author uses the verse rebuking those who say God has a son to support the human creation of actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'an's rebuke of those who say God has a son reinforces the argument that human actions are created by humans.

Core Idea
What God condemns, He does not create.

The author strengthens his argument by analyzing a verse that rebukes the claim that God has a son. If that blasphemous statement were created by God, the rebuke would be absurd. This shows that the statement must be the creation of the speaker.

Guided Path
1
Read the additional verse passage
Read the Arabic text starting from 'ومما يؤكد ذلك' through the end. Then read the translation.
This part uses the verse from Surah Maryam about those who say God has a son.
2
Understand the first aspect of inference
If the blasphemous statement were created by God, then God would be rebuking Himself indirectly. The Qur'anic estimation would be absurd: 'the heavens almost split because of what I created in the servant and intended.'
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
3
Understand the second aspect
The verse explicitly says 'You have come with something monstrous' (lā qad ji'tum shay'an iddan), attributing the action to the servant. Also, if God were to rebuke an action He Himself created, He would be foolish.
The second aspect combines textual attribution and logical consistency.
4
Connect back to the main argument
This additional proof reinforces the conclusion that human actions must be created by the servant, as divine rebuke of an act implies the act is not God's.

This passage presents a proof that human actions are created by the servant (ʿabd), not by God. The author begins by stating that the Qur'an contains verses indicating that when a servant performs an action, God recompenses him with another action. From this, the author argues that such recompense implies the action must be the servant's own creation, not God's. This is broken into two premises. Verses and Rejoinder: The Argument from Will
Author presents objection verses and responds with a rejoinder about will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author turns the opponents' proof texts into evidence for his own position by focusing on the relationship between human will and divine will.

Core Idea
The same verses can be read to prove that all actions depend on Allah's will.

Opponents of the Ash'ari view on qadar often cite Quranic verses that seem to grant humans independent choice. In this passage, the author presents these very verses and then offers a rejoinder that flips their meaning. Instead of proving human autonomy, the author argues, these verses actually prove that human action is subordinate to divine will because they link action to will, and the human will is attached to Allah's will. Let's examine this closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection: the verses
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully to see the five verses the opponents use to argue for human free will. Notice the wording that seems to give humans control over their choices.
These verses are classic proof texts for those who believe in human free will.
2
Understand the rejoinder
The author responds that these verses actually support his position. Identify the key logical move: the verses attribute action to the will, and the servant's will is attached to Allah's will.
The rejoinder hinges on the concept of 'ta'lil al-fi'l bi al-mashi'a' (attributing action to the will).
3
Trace the logical chain
Follow the author's reasoning: verses → action depends on will → human will depends on Allah's will → therefore action depends on Allah's will. This chain shows that the verses do not prove independent human power.
4
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
Many readers initially think these verses support free will. The misconception is that human choice is absolute. The author corrects this by showing the subordinate role of human will.
This lesson guards against reading the verses in isolation from the broader theological framework.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الثامن القوم
الآيات الدالة على كون العبد متمكناً من الإيمان والكفر ، قادراً على الخير والشر.
قال تعالى : ( فمن شاء فليؤمن ، ومن شاء فليكفر ) وقال : ( لمن شاء منكم أن يستقيم ) وقال : ( إنا هديناه السبيل ، إما شاكراً وإما كفوراً ) وقال : ( وهديناه النجدين ) أي طريقي الخير والشر . وقال : ونفس وما سواها. فألهمها فجورها وتقواها ( والجواب : إنا ذكرنا هذه الآيات دليلاً لنا . لأنها تقتضي تعليل الفعل . بالمشيئة . ومشيئة العبد معلقة بمشيئة الله تعالى ، فيكون فعل العبد معلقاً بمشيئة الله تعالى . من هذا الوجه
The eighth type: the people/statement? The verses indicating that the servant is capable of faith and disbelief, able to do good and evil. He, may He be exalted, said: 'So whoever wills, let him believe, and whoever wills, let him disbelieve.' And He said: 'For whoever among you wills to be upright.' And He said: 'Indeed, We guided him to the way, whether grateful or ungrateful.' And He said: 'And We guided him to the two paths' meaning the two ways of good and evil. And He said: 'And [by] the soul and He who proportioned it. And inspired it [with discernment of] its wickedness and its righteousness.' (And the response: We have mentioned these verses as evidence for us. Because they necessitate that the action is attributed to the will. And the will of the servant is attached to the will of Allah, the Exalted, so the action of the servant is attached to the will of Allah, the Exalted, from this aspect.)
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer. The objector cites several Quranic verses that appear to affirm human free will and the ability to choose faith or disbelief, good or evil. These verses include: 'Whoever wills, let him believe; whoever wills, let him disbelieve' (18:29), 'For whoever among you wills to be upright' (81:28), 'We guided him to the way, whether grateful or ungrateful' (76:3), 'We guided him to the two paths' (90:10), and the verse about the soul and its inspiration of wickedness and righteousness (91:7-8). The author then gives the response (al-jawab): these very verses are actually evidence for the author's position, not against it. The reason is that these verses attribute the action to the will (mashi'a). But the servant's will is dependent on and attached to Allah's will (mashi'at al-'abd mu'allaqa bi-mashi'at Allah ta'ala). Therefore, the servant's action is ultimately dependent on Allah's will. So the verses do not prove independent human power; they prove that human action is subordinate to divine will.

Key Terms
مشيئة (mashi'a)
تعليل الفعل (ta'lil al-fi'l)
فعل العبد (fi'l al-'abd)
مشيئة الله (mashi'at Allah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think these verses prove complete human free will and that humans are independent in their actions.
Correction: The author shows that the very same verses, when analyzed properly, lead to the opposite conclusion: because actions are tied to will, and the servant's will depends on Allah's will, all actions are ultimately under Allah's control.

Checkpoint
According to the author's response, why do the cited verses actually support his position?
A) Because they deny human ability altogether.
B) Because they attribute action to the will, and the servant's will is attached to Allah's will.
C) Because they mention both faith and disbelief.
D) Because they were revealed in Mecca.

Key Takeaway
The very verses opponents use to argue for free will actually demonstrate that human action is subordinate to divine will through the chain of will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every action you take is ultimately dependent on Allah's will, how does that change the way you view your own accomplishments and failures? Do you still credit yourself for your good deeds, or do you realize they are only by His will? Tonight, list three good deeds and say 'This is by the will of Allah' before sleeping.
?
The very verses you might have used to claim your independence are actually evidence of your dependence. In what areas of your life do you still feel you are in control? Ask Allah to show you your absolute need for His will in every breath, and commit to a day where you consciously attribute every choice to His will.
?
When you sin, do you blame your own free will, or do you acknowledge that even your sin occurs within Allah's ultimate decree? How does this affect your repentance? Determine to seek forgiveness tonight with the awareness that only by His will can you truly change.

Verses on Human Will and the Kalam Answer
Author enumerates verses on human will and gives kalam answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author of Al-Matalib al-Aliyah interprets Quranic verses that seem to affirm human free will, and how he reconciles them with the doctrine of divine predestination by linking the servant's will to Allah's will.

Core Idea
The servant's will is not independent; it is attached to Allah's will.

This lesson examines a key passage from Al-Matalib al-Aliyah where the author presents several Quranic verses that appear to give humans the power to choose faith or disbelief. He then offers a concise answer that transforms these verses into evidence for divine omnipotence by showing that every human will is contingent upon Allah's will. Let us explore how this reasoning works.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the full argument in the author's own words.
Notice the structure: first the verses, then the answer.
2
Identify the five Quranic verses
Locate each verse quoted and note what they seem to say about human ability. The verses are from Surah Kahf, Takwir, Insan, Balad, and Shams.
The verses consistently use phrases like 'whoever wills' and 'guided him'.
3
Examine the answer (الجواب)
Read the answer carefully. The author argues that these verses actually support his position because they attribute actions to will, and the servant's will is attached to Allah's will.
Focus on the phrase 'ومشيئة العبد معلقة بمشيئة الله'.
4
Understand the reconciliation
Reflect on how the answer resolves the apparent conflict. The servant has a real will, but it is not independent; it is always subject to Allah's overarching will.
This is a classic kalam solution to the problem of human free will versus divine predestination.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الثامن القوم
الآيات الدالة على كون العبد متمكناً من الإيمان والكفر، قادراً على الخير والشر.
قال تعالى: (فمن شاء فليؤمن، ومن شاء فليكفر) وقال: (لمن شاء منكم أن يستقيم) وقال: (إنا هديناه السبيل، إما شاكراً وإما كفوراً) وقال: (وهديناه النجدين) أي طريقي الخير والشر. وقال: (ونفس وما سواها. فألهمها فجورها وتقواها)
والجواب: إنا ذكرنا هذه الآيات دليلاً لنا. لأنها تقتضي تعليل الفعل بالمشيئة. ومشيئة العبد معلقة بمشيئة الله تعالى، فيكون فعل العبد معلقاً بمشيئة الله تعالى. من هذا الوجه.
The eighth type: the people [or The eighth type: the saying] The verses indicating that the servant is capable of faith and disbelief, able to do good and evil. He said, the Most High: 'So whoever wills, let him believe, and whoever wills, let him disbelieve.' And He said: 'For whoever among you wills to be upright.' And He said: 'Indeed, We guided him to the way, whether he be grateful or ungrateful.' And He said: 'And We guided him to the two paths' meaning the two ways of good and evil. And He said: 'And [by] the soul and He who proportioned it, and inspired it [with discernment of] its wickedness and its righteousness.' And the answer: We have mentioned these verses as evidence for us. Because they necessitate attributing the action to the will. And the will of the servant is attached to the will of Allah, the Most High, so the action of the servant is attached to the will of Allah, the Most High, from this aspect.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage is a combination of evidence presentation and an answer to a potential objection. The author first introduces a type (likely the eighth type of evidence) consisting of verses that seem to affirm human free will and capacity for faith and disbelief. He quotes several Quranic verses that explicitly give the servant a choice: 'So whoever wills, let him believe...' (18:29), 'For whoever among you wills to be upright' (81:28), 'Indeed, We guided him to the way...' (76:3), 'And We guided him to the two paths' (90:10) meaning good and evil, and the famous verse from Surah Ash-Shams (91:7-8) where Allah inspired the soul with its wickedness and righteousness. The author then gives an answer (الجواب) that reconciles these verses with the doctrine of divine predestination. He explains that these verses actually serve as evidence for the author's own position because they ground actions in will (المشيئة). Specifically, the attribution of actions to the will of the servant is not independent; rather, the will of the servant is itself attached to and dependent upon the will of Allah. Therefore, the action of the servant is ultimately linked to Allah's will. The phrase 'from this aspect' (من هذا الوجه) indicates that this is one particular angle of reasoning, acknowledging that human actions are neither purely autonomous nor completely divorced from divine causality. The answer thus defends the compatibility of human capacity with divine omnipotence.

Key Terms
تمكين العبد
مشيئة العبد
مشيئة الله
تعليل الفعل
الآيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These verses prove that humans have an independent will that is not subject to Allah's will.
Correction: The answer shows that the servant's will is attached to Allah's will, so the servant's will is not independent.

Checkpoint
According to the answer (الجواب) in this passage, how is the servant's will related to Allah's will?
A) The servant's will is independent of Allah's will.
B) The servant's will is attached to Allah's will.
C) The servant has no will at all.
D) The verses are rejected as evidence.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic verses that seemingly affirm human free will are reconciled by affirming that the servant's will itself is dependent on and attached to Allah's will.

?

?

?
The answer in this lesson reconciles verses that seem to give you full control with the reality of divine decree. How does this reconciliation affect your sense of responsibility for your actions? Are you more or less accountable? How will this understanding change your attitude towards sin and obedience?

Three Qur'anic Proofs Against Vain Creation and an Objection
Three verses proving creation is not in vain, with an objection and answer regarding false sects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how three Qur'anic verses prove that creation is not vain, and how the objection from false sects is answered by the principle of divine dominion.

Core Idea
God's creation is true and just; apparent disparities are all within His dominion.

In this lesson, we examine three consecutive Qur'anic proofs that creation is purposeful, not play or vain. Then we confront a powerful objection: what about the existence of false sects and corrupt beliefs? The answer reveals a foundational principle of divine justice: God's actions in His own dominion are always right.

Guided Path
1
Read the three verses
Read the Arabic of each verse together with its translation. Notice the key terms: 'عبث' (vain), 'تفاوت' (disparity), 'ملك' (dominion).
These verses are from Surah al-Dukhan, al-Mu'minun, and al-Mulk.
2
Understand the proofs
Each verse refutes the idea that creation is without purpose. Identify how each verse emphasizes truth, purpose, and perfection.
3
Analyze the objection
The objection points to false sects and corrupt beliefs as evidence of disparity in creation. Understand why this seems to contradict the verse from al-Mulk.
The objection claims that if God created these sects, there would be disparity (تفاوت) in His creation.
4
Grasp the answer
The answer invokes the principle that the owner of a dominion can act freely, and all His actions are just. Since everything is God's dominion, His actions are always true and correct.
This answer does not deny the existence of false sects but asserts that their creation is just from God's perspective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وخامسها ؛ قوله : ( افحسبتم انما خلقناكم عبثاً) (2) .

And the fourth: His statement, exalted is He: 'And We did not create the heavens and the earth and what is between them in play; We did not create them except with truth.' Commentary
This passage presents three Qur'anic proofs that creation is not in vain, then raises an objection and answers it. The author lists three consecutive verses: (1) Surah al-Dukhan 44:38-39, stating that creation is not play but with truth; (2) Surah al-Mu'minun 23:115, asking if humans were created in vain; and (3) Surah al-Mulk 67:3, noting no disparity in the Most Merciful's creation. The objection argues that the existence of corrupt beliefs and false sects shows severe disparity, and if these sects were created by God, that would imply disparity in His creation. The answer affirms that God's actions in His own dominion are always just, correct, and free from falsehood and vanity. Since all creation is His dominion, every action of His is truth and correctness. Thus, any apparent disparity from human perspective does not detract from divine justice.

The answer to the objection shows that God's creation of all things, including apparent disparities from false sects, is just because He is the Owner of all creation.

Evidence from Surah Aal-e-Imran: Human Actions Not from Allah
A Qur'anic argument using Surah Aal-e-Imran 3:78 to refute the idea that evil actions come from Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'anic verse about Jewish distortion of scripture (Surah Aal-e-Imran 3:78) is used as a logical proof that false speech and evil actions are not created by Allah.

Core Idea
If false speech were from Allah, the Jews would be truthful, but Allah denies it.

This lesson examines the eleventh type of Qur'anic evidence that human actions are not created by Allah. The passage focuses on Surah Aal-e-Imran 3:78, which describes Jews twisting their tongues with the Book and falsely claiming it is from Allah. The argument is sharp: if their distortion were created by Allah, then their claim would be true, but Allah explicitly refutes it. Understanding this inference clarifies the Islamic position that evil actions are not attributable to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the verse
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the verse cited (Surah Aal-e-Imran 3:78) and the key claim that the Jews said 'It is from Allah' while it is not.
The verse describes a specific act of distortion (tahrif) by a group of Jews.
2
Understand the logical inference
The passage presents a conditional argument: if distortion and lying were created by Allah, then the Jews would be truthful in saying their distortion is from Allah. But Allah denies it, so the condition is false.
This is a classical reductio ad absurdum.
3
Reflect on al-Jubba'i's remark
Al-Jubba'i comments that this reasoning suffices to shame those who would consider the Jews more truthful than Allah. Think about the rhetorical weight of this statement.
Al-Jubba'i was a prominent Mu'tazili theologian.
4
Consider the anticipated objection
The passage begins to address an objection: that when the Jews said 'it is from Allah' they meant it was the speech of Allah. The text cuts off, but the implied response is that the Quran is Allah's speech, not their distortion.
The objection attempts to reinterpret the verse to avoid the conclusion.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The way of inference from the verse: that if distortion and lying in the tongue were a creation of Allah Almighty, then the Jews would be truthful in their saying that it is from Allah, and Allah would not have contradicted them in His statement: 'And it is not from Allah.' This passage introduces the eleventh type of Qur'anic evidence that human actions are not created by Allah. It cites Surah Aal-e-Imran 3:78, which describes Jews twisting their tongues with the Book and falsely claiming it is from Allah. The argument proceeds: if distortion and lying were created by Allah, then the Jews would be telling the truth when they say their distortion is from Allah, but Allah explicitly denies it by saying 'it is not from Allah.' Therefore, such false actions cannot be from Allah. The passage then quotes al-Jubba'i, who says this reasoning suffices to shame those who would consider the Jews more truthful than Allah. Finally, an anticipated objection is introduced: it might be said that the Jews' statement 'it is from Allah' means the distorted speech is the speech of Allah; but the text cuts off before the full response.

Refuting Determinist Readings of Two Verses
Author refutes determinist readings of two verses by distinguishing negation of ruling from negation of creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the determinist (Jabariyya) interpretation of two Qur'anic verses by distinguishing between negation of a legal ruling and negation of God's creative act.

Core Idea
The verses deny pagan rulings, not that God creates all things.

This passage tackles a key proof used by determinists (Jabariyya) who claim that certain Qur'anic verses prove God creates all actions, including human acts. The author shows that these verses actually negate legal rulings (hukm) and human authority, not the act of creation itself. By analyzing the words 'ja'ala' and 'sultan', he demonstrates that the determinist reading misconstrues the divine attribute of creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Notice the two distinct verse references and the author's counter-argument.
Pay attention to the bracketed phrase which may be a marginal variant.
2
Understand the first verse (bahira/sa'ibah)
Identify the determinists' claim: that the verse 'ma ja'ala' negates God's act of creation. The author counters that it negates a legal ruling (hukm) only, not creation.
The key is the word 'ja'ala' which can mean to make a ruling or to create.
3
Analyze the second verse (names/sultan)
The author argues that if the idols were God's creation, He would have sent down the greatest authority (sultan) for them. Since He did not, they are not His creation.
Focus on the linguistic derivation: sultan from tasallut (domination), and the highest domination is bringing into existence.
4
Synthesize the refutation
Reflect on how both arguments share a common method: reinterpreting the verse to negate human legal authority rather than divine creative act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن الآيات التي يتمسكون بها من هذا الجنس قوله تعالى : ( ما جعل من بحيرة ولا سائبة ) وعندنا : المراد نفي الحكم [ وعندهم : المراد نفي الحكم ] والخلق معاً الله . والآية الثالثة من هذا الجنس قوله تعالى : ( إن هي إلا أسماء سميتموها . أنتم وآباؤكم . ما أنزل الله بها من سلطان ) ولو كان ذلك من خلقه ، لكان قد أنزل الله بها أعظم وجوه السلطان . لأن السلطان مشتق من التسلط ، ولا تسلط فوق الإيجاد، والإخراج من العدم إلى الوجود .
And among the verses they cling to of this kind is His statement: 'He has not made (ma ja'ala) a bahirah or a sa'ibah.' According to us: the intended meaning is negation of the ruling [according to them: the intended meaning is negation of the ruling] and the creation together. And the third verse of this kind is His statement: 'They are nothing but names which you have named, you and your fathers; Allah has sent down no authority (sultan) for them.' And if that were from His creation, then He would have sent down for them the greatest of authorities (wujuh al-sultan). Because al-sultan is derived from al-tasallut (domination), and there is no domination above bringing into existence (al-ijad) and bringing forth from non-existence to existence.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the determinist (Jabariyya) interpretation of two specific Qur'anic verses. The author begins by stating that these are among the verses the determinists use to support their claim that God creates all actions, including human acts. The first verse is 'ma ja'ala Allahu min bahirah wa la sa'ibah' (He has not made a bahirah or a sa'ibah) – referring to pagan practices regarding cattle. The determinists argue that this shows God creates (ja'ala) these things. The author counters that the intended meaning is negation of a legal ruling (nafi al-hukm), not negation of the act of creation (al-khalq). The phrase 'according to them' is a variant indicating the determinists' view that both ruling and creation are negated. The second verse is 'in hiya illa asma' sammaytumoha...' (They are but names you have named... Allah has sent down no authority for them). The author argues: if these idols or objects of worship were created by God, then He would have sent down the greatest authority (sultan) for them, because 'sultan' is derived from 'tasallut' (domination), and there is no greater domination than bringing into existence (ijad) from non-existence. Since God did not send down such authority, these things cannot be His creation – they are merely human fabrications. The logic is that if God had created them, He would have given them the highest proof of His sovereignty, which is the act of creation itself. The argument refutes the deterministic reading by showing that the verses actually deny that these things are God's creation, because if they were, God would have made that evident through the supreme authority of His creative act.

Key Terms
بحيرة
سائبة
سلطان
إيجاد
تسلط
نفي الحكم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The determinists think the verses prove God creates all actions, including pagan practices and idols.
Correction: The verses actually negate legal rulings (hukm) and human authority, not the act of creation.

Checkpoint

A) It proves God creates all actions directly.
B) It negates a legal ruling only.
C) It refers to the creation of the universe.
D) It is abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The determinist reading misinterprets verses as negating creation when they actually negate human legal authority.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just seen that determinists twist verses to claim that God creates all things, including your own choices. Are there areas in your life where you blame 'qadr' for your own neglect, lack of effort, or even sin? If so, this lesson exposes that as a misreading. Will you today repent for using God's decree as a shield and instead take full ownership of your actions?
?
The pagans named their idols and claimed authority for them—but God did not create them. In your own life, what 'names' have you given to your habits, addictions, or worldly pursuits that grant them authority over you, even though God never created them as such? This lesson teaches that only God's creation carries true authority. Are you ready to break the false authority you have granted to things that are not of God?
?
The author argues that if something were God's creation, He would have given it the greatest authority—the very act of bringing into existence. Think of your own faith: Do you treat God's creation (like the Qur'an, the Prophet, the signs in the universe) with the reverence they deserve as His authority? Or have you become desensitized to His signs, treating them as ordinary? This lesson calls you to reawaken your awe before the fact that everything that exists is a direct act of His power. How will you increase your mindfulness of His creative authority today?

Objection and Answer on Divine Intention and Human Action
Objection from Quranic verses and Ash'ari answer on divine intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'ari response resolves the apparent contradiction between Quranic verses showing God's purpose for obedience and the doctrine that God creates all actions, including disbelief.

Core Idea
God's intention for obedience is fulfilled ultimately in the hereafter, not immediately in every person.

This passage engages a classic objection against predestination: if God creates disbelief, how can He genuinely intend obedience? The objector marshals several Quranic verses to argue that God's purpose would be contradictory. The Ash'ari answer reframes the issue by distinguishing between immediate and ultimate fulfillment. Let's examine the argument and its resolution.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the verses cited
Begin by reading the entire passage, noting the verses the objector uses (4:64, 51:56, 6:51, 20:44). Follow the logic that God's purpose seems impossible if He creates disbelief.
The verses are explicit about God wanting obedience and piety.
2
Identify the logical problem
Understand the contradiction: if God creates disbelief in humans, then His purpose in sending prophets (to be obeyed) and in creating humans (to worship) would be thwarted. The objector argues this is incoherent.
The phrases 'perhaps' (لعل) are used to imply contingency.
3
Study the Ash'ari answer
Focus on the response: 'an affirmative proposition suffices by the occurrence of a named thing from one time.' This means God's intention for obedience is not required to occur immediately or in every individual; it is enough that it occurs at some point.
The answer introduces a temporal dimension to divine intention.
4
Understand ultimate fulfillment
The passage concludes that God will make everyone a believer and a knower 'in the final end' (القيمة). Thus, His intention for obedience is ultimately realized in the hereafter, resolving the apparent contradiction.
This shifts the focus from this world to the afterlife.
5
Reflect on the resolution
Consider how this response defends Ash'ari predestination without denying the Quranic verses. The key is that God's will is not confined to immediate outcomes.
This is a common Ash'ari approach to harmonizing verses with qadar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التنوع الرابع علم اللقيم
قوله تعالى : ( وما أرسلنا من رسول إلا ليطاع بإذن الله )
دلت الآية على أن مقصوده تعالى من بعثة الأنبياء إقدام الخلق على الطاعة . فلو كان تعالى يخلق الكفر فيهم ، لامتنع أن يكون غرضه من البعثة حصول الطاعة . وهذا التمسك بقوله تعالى : ( وما خلقت الجن والإنس إلا ليعبدون ) وهكذا الاستدلال بكل ما جاء في القرآن من قوله : ( لعلهم يتقون ) - ( فقولا له : قولاً ليناً . لعله يتذكر أو يخشى ) فإن هذه النصوص وما يشبهها نصوص صريحة في أنه تعالى يريد من عباده فعل الطاعة والتقوى ولو كانت الطاعة والتقوى من خلق الله تعالى لكان يجب أن يقول : لعلي أتذكر وأتقي
والجواب : إن القضية الموجبة يكفي في العمل بها ، حصول مسمى من وقت واحد وعندنا : أنه تعالى يجعل الكل مؤمناً عارفاً في القيمة
The fourth type: the science of al-luqaym [?]. His saying, exalted is He: 'And We sent not a messenger except to be obeyed by permission of Allah.' The verse indicates that His purpose, exalted is He, from sending the prophets is the creatures' undertaking of obedience. So if He, exalted is He, were to create disbelief in them, it would be impossible that His purpose from the sending would be the attainment of obedience. And this is holding fast to His saying, exalted is He: 'And I created not the jinn and mankind except that they worship Me.' And similarly the inference from every [verse] that came in the Qur'an of His saying: 'that they may fear' and 'Speak to him with gentle speech that perhaps he may be reminded or fear.' For these texts and what resembles them are explicit texts that He, exalted is He, wills from His servants the act of obedience and piety. And if obedience and piety were from the creation of Allah, exalted is He, then it would have been necessary that He say: 'perhaps I may be reminded and fear.' And the answer: Indeed, the affirmative proposition suffices in acting upon it, the occurrence of a named [thing] from one time. And with us: that He, exalted is He, makes everyone a believer and a knower in the final end.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage presents an objection against the Ash'ari doctrine that God creates human actions (including disbelief), and then provides the Ash'ari response. The objector cites several Quranic verses: 'And We sent not a messenger except to be obeyed by permission of Allah' (4:64), 'And I created not the jinn and mankind except that they worship Me' (51:56), 'that they may fear' (6:51), and 'Speak to him with gentle speech that perhaps he may be reminded or fear' (20:44). The argument is that these verses show God's purpose in sending prophets and creating humans is to produce obedience and piety. If God Himself were to create disbelief in them, then His purpose would be contradicted—He would be working against His own intention. Moreover, the verses imply that the outcome (obedience or fear) depends on human choice, not divine creation; otherwise the phrase 'perhaps' would apply to God Himself. The answer reframes the issue: an affirmative proposition (e.g., 'God intends obedience') is satisfied as long as its object occurs at some time; it does not require immediate or universal fulfillment. The Ash'ari position holds that ultimately, in the hereafter, God will make every person a believer and a knower, thus fulfilling His intention absolutely. Therefore, the objection fails because it assumes that the purpose must be realized in this world without exception, whereas the Ash'aris affirm that it will be realized in the final state.

Key Terms
إقدام الخلق على الطاعة
خلق الكفر
القضية الموجبة
القيمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quranic verses prove that God's will for obedience is always fulfilled immediately in this world, so He cannot create disbelief.
Correction: The verses indicate God's purpose, but the Ash'aris explain that His intention is satisfied ultimately in the hereafter, not necessarily immediately in every individual. God's creating disbelief does not contradict His intention because the intention will be fully realized in the final end.

Checkpoint
According to the answer given in this passage, why does God's intention for obedience not conflict with His creating disbelief?
A) Because God only intends obedience for believers, not disbelievers.
B) Because the affirmative proposition is satisfied by occurrence at one time, and God will make all believers in the hereafter.
C) Because the Quranic verses are metaphorical and do not indicate a real intention.
D) Because disbelief is not created by God, so there is no conflict.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari response shows that God's intention for obedience is satisfied in the ultimate sense, as He will make all believers in the hereafter.

?

Proof from Quran 35:37 and Reply to the Compulsion Objection
Author presents a proof from Quran 35:37 and answers an objection about compulsion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'anic verse 35:37 is used to argue for human responsibility, and why the objection of compulsion (jabr) is self-defeating.

Core Idea
The Qur'an's argument presupposes human ability, so the objection of compulsion undermines itself.

In this passage, the author presents one of the most sophisticated arguments in the debate on divine predestination and human free will. He cites a Qur'anic verse where God addresses the disbelievers, reminding them of the opportunities they were given. Then he anticipates the objection that if God creates everything, then faith and disbelief are from God, making the divine argument meaningless. Finally, he exposes the incoherence in the objector's position. Let's follow this logical chain step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Qur'anic proof
Read the verse and the author's explanation of how it serves as evidence that humans had ability and opportunity.
Notice the four elements: ability, enablement, long life, and the warner.
2
Identify the objection
The passage says: if faith and reflection were created by God, the disbelievers could blame God. Identify this potential retort.
The objector cites Quran 6:149 to argue that God's argument would be invalid.
3
Grasp the answer
The author replies that the objection is problematic for the objector, because act depends on power and motive, leading to compulsion, and also contradicts God's foreknowledge.
This shows the objection is self-defeating.
4
Reflect on the principle
Consider how the author uses the objector's own reasoning to turn the tables, demonstrating that the objection would force the objector into an even worse position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الخامس عشر القيم
قوله تعالى : ( أو لم نعمركم ما يتذكر فيه من تذكر ، وجاءكم النذير (١)
ووجه الاستدلال : إنه تعالى احتج عليهم بالتمكن والإقدار ، والعمر الطويل ، والمهلة في أوقات التكليف ، وإزاحة الأعذار ببعثة الرسل . فلو كان الإيمان والتذكر موقوفين على خلق الله ، لكان لهم أن يقولوا : الهتنا قد فعلت فينا الكفر ، والعدول عن طاعتك ، وكنا عاجزين عن دفع ما خلقت ، ولم تخلق فينا الإيمان . ولو خلقت الإيمان فينا لكنا مؤمنين بك . قالوا : فكيف يعقل أن يحتج الله سبحانه عليهم بما لا حجة له فيه ، مع أنه قال : ( قل فلله الحجة البالغة (٢) ) ؟ وليس لهم أن يقولوا : المناظرة مع الله لا تجوز . لأن هذا الكلام قد سبق جوابه .
والجواب : إن كل ذلك مشكل عليهم ، بما أن حصول الفعل موقوف على خلق [القدرة و(٣)] الداعي وذلك يوجب الجبر ، ويشكل أيضاً . بما أن خلاف معلوم الله محال الوقوع .
The fifteenth type: al-qayyam (values?)
His saying, exalted is He: (Did We not give you long life enough for him who would reflect to reflect? And there came to you the warner [35:37])
The aspect of the proof: He, exalted, argued against them by [their] ability and enablement, the long life, the respite during times of obligation, and the removal of excuses by sending messengers. For if faith and reflection were dependent on God's creation, they would have said: Our God, You have caused disbelief in us, and turning away from Your obedience, and we were incapable of repelling what You created, and You did not create faith in us. And had You created faith in us, we would have been believers in You. They said: How is it reasonable that God, exalted, argues against them with something in which He has no argument, while He said: (Say: To God belongs the conclusive argument [6:149])? And they cannot say: Disputation with God is not permissible. Because this speech has already been answered before.
The answer: All of that is problematic for them, because the occurrence of the act depends on the creation of [power and (3)] the motive, and that necessitates compulsion, and it is also problematic because that which is contrary to God's knowledge is impossible of occurrence.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage presents a proof from the Qur'an, followed by an objection and an answer. The proof is based on Quran 35:37, where God argues against the disbelievers that they were given long life and a warner, so they have no excuse. The author explains that if faith (iman) and reflection were dependent on God's direct creation, the disbelievers could object that God Himself caused their disbelief and did not create faith in them. They ask how God could argue against them if He were the cause of their disbelief, citing the verse 'Say: To God belongs the conclusive argument.' The author then notes that the objection that disputation with God is not permissible has already been answered.

The answer is that this objection is actually problematic for the objectors themselves, because the occurrence of any act depends on the creation of power (qudra) and the motive (da'i), which implies compulsion (jabr). Thus their own position is also subject to the same difficulty. Additionally, it is impossible for an act to occur contrary to God's foreknowledge. So the objection is self-defeating.

Correction: The verse actually presupposes human ability, and the objection that it implies compulsion is self-defeating because the objector's own position leads to the same problem.

Key Takeaway
The argument from Qur'an 35:37 demonstrates that God holds humans accountable based on the abilities He granted them, and the objection that this implies compulsion fails because it would also undermine the objector's own stance.
